حال ، ثم كانت الأعراض لأنفسها لا تقوم ولا تقدح في الأشياء ، ثبت أنها عملت فيها هذا العمل بمن يعلم أنها تعمل كذا ، ولم يجز أن يكون يعلم أحد ذلك إلا بمن يملك جعل تلك الجواهر يصلح لاحتمال تلك الأعراض ، ومحال علم مثله إلا بمن يجعلها كذلك ، وفى ذلك لزوم القول بواحد عليم قادر لا يخفى عليه شيء ولا يصعب عليه تكوين ما يريد كونه . وإن كانت أعراضا فمحال وجودها لأنفسها وقيامها ، فلزم القول بموجد قديم ، مع إيجاد ما فيه وبه يدخل في حد الوجود . على أن حدث الأعراض مما لا نمانع فيه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله وبعد ، فإنه معلوم أن تلك الطبائع هي متضادة ، وحق التضاد التدافع وفي ذلك تفرق ، وفي التفرق تبدد وتفان ، فلم يحتمل أن يكون أصول الأشياء لأنفسها كائنة وقائمة مع التناقض الذي ذكرت ، ثبت أنها إن كانت كانت يمانع عن التدافع الذي فيه التبدد ، وهو الجامع بينها بعد التفرق ، القاهر لها ، وبالمجمع كان العالم ، ثبت حدوثه . وفي ذلك فساد القول بالطبائع لأن كون شيء لا عن شيء ليس بأبعد في العقول من قيام الشيء مع صده وهو ما ينقضه ، ولبعد ذلك عن عقولهم صاروا إلى ما قالوا ، فإذا لزمهم فيما قالوا مثل الذي عنه فروا بطل قولهم وذهب عذرهم ... وبالله العصمة
If [natures] mixed by themselves, they would produce an ugly color, which reason counts as corruption of dyes. But if a wise, knowing chemist mixes them, knowing the outcomes of that mixture, it comes out perfect and good. Then since the world came out perfect, it is established that the One by whom the world exists is Knowing, Wise, aware of the outcomes of things, so He brought them out accordingly. In that is the corruption of [the claim] that these natures, or clay, or whatever names they named themselves [with act] by themselves, such that [the world] comes out as it does. So it is established that the One who originated them thus is a wise manager, and they must be originated not from something. Moreover, the colors—every one of them—is not described by anything of what they mentioned of heat and cold; for there may be among things one dominated by a color while being hot, and another dominated by that [same color] while being cold. So it is established that none of those colors [correspond to] what they mentioned, nor what they mentioned by them. In that is an affirmation other than what they said. And with Allah is success. Likewise one finds the tastes in them varying, such that with one color and one nature it comes out in a type of taste, like saltiness, sourness, bitterness, or clay that does not incline to any of that. It is established that that was by the management of One Who has power to make each as He wills without causes. And there is no power except with Allah. These natures cannot but be either atoms or accidents. If they are atoms, they are affected by the accidents that occur in them as mentioned—of difference, combination, and separation. Without these, every atom would be separate. And the difference of atoms with the combination of mixtures in them indicates the dominance of accidents over them, and that they turn them from state to state. Then the accidents by themselves do not subsist and do not affect things. [Thus] it is established that they performed this action in them by one who knows that they act thus. And it is not permissible that anyone know that except by one who has power to make those atoms suitable for receiving those accidents. And knowledge of that is impossible except by one who makes them thus. In that is the necessity of affirming one Knowing, Able [God] from whom nothing is hidden and for whom the bringing into being of what He wills is not difficult. And if they are accidents, their existence by themselves and their subsistence is impossible, so affirmation of an eternal originator is necessitated, along with the bringing into being of what is in it and by which it enters the limit of existence. Moreover, the occurrence of accidents is something we do not dispute. And there is no power except with Allah. Later: it is known that these natures are mutually opposed; and the requirement of opposition is mutual repulsion, and in that is dispersion, and in dispersion is disintegration and annihilation. So it is impossible that the origins of things be by themselves subsisting and enduring with the contradiction I mentioned. [Thus] it is established that if they were [to exist], they would be prevented from the mutual repulsion which entails disintegration—He is the one who gathers them after dispersion, the subduer of them. And by the gathered [world] the world came to be; its temporality is established. In that is the corruption of the doctrine of natures, because the existence of something from nothing is not more remote in reason than the existence of a thing along with what opposes it—i.e., what contradicts it. And because that was remote to their minds, they resorted to what they said. So when they are bound by what they said to something like that which they fled from, their doctrine is falsified and their excuse is gone. And with Allah is protection.
Source pages p. 741

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument (proof) refuting the theory that the world arises from self-acting natures (طبائع) and proving the existence of a wise, powerful creator. The argument proceeds in the following order: First, the author uses an analogy of dyes: if colors are mixed by themselves, they produce ugly results; but if mixed by a wise chemist, the result is perfect. Similarly, the world is well-ordered, so its maker must be wise. Second, he notes that colors and tastes are not tied to a single nature: the same nature can yield different colors or tastes, disproving the claim that natures produce fixed effects by themselves. This randomness shows they are not self-sufficient. Third, he examines whether natures are atoms (جواهر) or accidents (أعراض). If atoms, they are shaped by accidents, and accidents require an external knower. If accidents, they cannot subsist alone, so an eternal creator is needed. Fourth, he argues that natures are inherently opposed, leading to repulsion and dispersion; but the world is unified, so there must be a unifier who overcomes this opposition. The conclusion is that the theory of natures collapses because it leads to the very absurdity its proponents sought to avoid—namely, explaining the world without a creator. The author finally invokes divine protection.

Key Terms
طبائع
حكيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is just an analogy without any empirical support.
Correction: Maturidi also provides an observation about colors and temperature that supports the analogy.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what would happen if dyes mixed by themselves?
A) They would produce beautiful colors.
B) They would produce ugly colors.
C) They would not mix at all.
D) They would produce no color.

Key Takeaway
The order and consistency in colors cannot result from blind natures; they require a wise, knowing creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the order in your own life—your health, family, and daily provision—do you truly attribute it to a wise Creator, or do you sometimes drift into thinking it is just luck or nature? How would acknowledging Allah's wisdom change how you respond to difficulties?
?
The analogy says a wise chemist produces perfect colors. Do you treat the world—your time, energy, and relationships—as a random mixture or as something entrusted to you by a Wise Manager? What would it look like to live consistently with that belief starting today?
?
The passage argues that colors are not tied to cold or heat. In what areas of your life do you wrongly assume that outward appearances are determined by fixed natures (e.g., assuming someone's actions are purely from their disposition)? How does this lesson call you to look beyond superficial causes and trust in the wisdom of Allah's design?

Taste Variation, Atoms, Accidents, and the Necessity of a Creator
Maturidi refutes natures by citing variation in tastes and analyzing their ontological status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's arguments that the variation of tastes in similar substances disproves self-acting natures, and that the analysis of natures as atoms or accidents leads to the necessity of an eternal creator.

Core Idea
Tastes and substances vary, pointing to a manager; and natures cannot be self-sufficient as either atoms or accidents.

Maturidi continues his refutation by pointing out that the same nature can produce different tastes, indicating an external cause. He then examines the nature of these 'natures' themselves: if they are atoms, they are shaped by accidents requiring a knower; if they are accidents, they cannot exist on their own. Finally, he argues that natures are opposed and would destroy each other without a unifier.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument about taste variation
Notice how Maturidi says that a single nature can yield different tastes (salty, sour, bitter, etc.), which would not happen if natures acted by themselves.
This observation points to an external manager.
2
Understand the atom hypothesis
Maturidi considers if natures are atoms (جواهر) and argues that they are shaped by accidents, which require a knowing agent to direct them.
Accidents themselves do not subsist, so they need a cause.
3
Understand the accident hypothesis
If natures are accidents (أعراض), they cannot exist independently, so an eternal originator is needed.
4
Grasp the opposition argument
Natures are mutually opposed, leading to repulsion and disintegration. The existence of a unified world shows there must be a unifier who overcomes this opposition.
This final argument seals the refutation.

The Astrologers' Claim and the Impossibility of an Infinite Past
Maturidi presents the astrologers' view and gives his first refutation regarding infinite motions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the astrologers' argument for eternal motions and Maturidi's first refutation showing that an infinite past series cannot be traversed, thus motions must have a beginning.

Core Idea
An infinite chain of past motions cannot reach the present; therefore, a beginning is necessary.

Maturidi begins by presenting the views of those who claim eternal motions, including the astrologers' elaborate analogy of the brocade weaver. He then launches his first argument: if motions have come to an end, they must have had a beginning, otherwise an infinite number of motions would have to be completed, which is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the astrologers' claims
Carefully read the first part of the Arabic passage where Maturidi describes the astrologers' position. Note their three main assertions.
The astrologers use an analogy of a brocade weaver to explain how stars govern the world.
2
Identify the three core claims
List the three claims: (1) things are eternal, (2) stars have always governed the world, (3) bodies are eternal and motions are accidents that occur infinitely.
These claims set the stage for Maturidi's refutation.
3
Trace Maturidi's first argument
Read Maturidi's first argument: every motion that has passed has an end, so if motions had no beginning, an infinite number would have ended—contradiction.
This argument relies on the impossibility of traversing an infinite series.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand that if motions have an end, they must have a beginning. This refutes the astrologers' claim of eternal motions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوم قالوا بمثل ذلك إلا أنهم زعموا أن ليس لأجناس [الطبائع] عدد يعرفونه ، وكلهم قالوا بقدم الأشياء فى جميع جملتها من مهب الشمال والجنوب والدبور والصبا ومن أعلاها وأسفلها متصلة به وزعم قوم من المنجمة أن النجوم لم تزل تدبر أمر العالم ، وهى ومنها سعد ، فاختلافه باختلاف ما اتصل به منها كأداة صاحب الديباج بالخيوط الموصولة من الإبر بسم بأعلى أداتها بما يظهر فيه من الظهور وغيره برفع الخشب وحفظها ، فمثله أمر النجوم بالعالم تختلف صورته باختلاف تحرك النجوم ، وفى اختلافها وائتلافها السعادة والنحس . وهي لم تزل تتحرك فيحدث من كل حركة غير الذي يحدث من غيرها ويتولد ذلك ، ويمثل ذلك يقولون في البيضة والدجاجة أنه يكون ذلك بضرب من حركات النجوم كالديباج الذي ذكرت . وزعموا أن الأجسام قديمة وهى غير الأعراض ، والحركات أعراض ، تحدث إلى ما لا نهاية لها ، وصيروا أمر جميع العالم اضطرارا بما كان كذلك بالنجوم والأفلاك من اجتماع وتفرق ، فمثله في النجوم نقول ، وبالله التوفيق . قال الشيخ رحمه الله : / أما القول بحركات لا نهاية لها فقد بينا فيما تقدم فسادها ، ما لا يشك في حركة انقضت إلا أنها نهاية ما تقدم من الحركات حتى لا يكون شيء مما تقدم بعد هذه ، وإذا ثبت نهاية الفناء لها والانقضاء هو كذلك، يجز أن يتناهى الاقتضاء لما لا يتناهى له الابتداء ، ثبت لذلك الابتداء . وبعد ، فإنا رأينا الجواهر كلها فى رأى العين متفاوتة الحدود ، لا يحتمل أن تكون هي كذلك، على غير أن تكون كذلك إلا عن أقل متفاوت يظهر في أكثره ذلك : فثبت أن كان لذلك عن أصغر خال يكون عظمة وكثافته بعد أن لم يكن ، ولطف عظمه وكثافته في الكون بعد أن لم يكن لا بشيء تقدمه ؛ لأن في التقديم ايجاب الاستواء ، وقد ثبت التفاوت ، فثبت أن الذي تقدم هو حدث بعد أن لم يكن ؛ إذ هو في معنى ما مع ما لو كانت الحركات إذ هي مستديرة لو جعلت مستقيمة من جهة ليكون بعضها على أثر بعض ، وفى وجود بعضها فناء البعض ، ولو وجب قديم الحركات ليجب قدم فنائها ، فتكون في الأزل معدومة موجودة ؛ وذلك متناقض ؛ إذ لا يجوز اجتماع الوجود والفناء في حال ، فكذا فى كل الأحوال ، وفى ذلك لزوم الابتداء . مع ما لو تفاوت - في رأي العين ذهاب سرعة . أحد سبق [آخر] ، يسيران سيرا مستقيما ، لا يحتمل أن لا يكون ابتداء أحدهما قبل ابتداء الآخر أو أحدهما أسرع الآخر ، وفى رفع النهاية عنها بطلان النهاية بينهما ، وفى بطلانه نقض المحسوس، ثبت لهما الابتداء ، وكذلك هذا المعنى ، وكذلك هذا المعنى فى المستدير من الحركات والله الموفق . وبهذا كله ننقض على جميع القائلين بقدم الأعيان ، غير خارجة عن الأعراض ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . و بمثله تكلم أصحاب الطبائع .
And a group said similarly, except that they claimed that the kinds of [natures] do not have a known number, and all of them said that things are eternal in their entirety, from the direction of the north, south, west, and east winds, and from their highest and lowest parts connected to it. And a group of astrologers claimed that the stars have never ceased to govern the affairs of the world, and they are, and among them is fortune. So its difference varies according to what is connected to it from them, like the tool of the brocade weaver with the threads connected from the needle to the top of his tool, by what appears in it of appearance and other, by raising the wood and preserving it. So similarly, the affair of the stars with the world: its form varies according to the movement of the stars, and in their difference and union there is good fortune and misfortune. And they have never ceased moving, so from each movement occurs something other than what occurs from another, and it is generated. And they give an example of the egg and the chicken, that this occurs by a kind of movements of the stars, like the brocade I mentioned. And they claimed that bodies are eternal and they are not accidents, and movements are accidents, occurring to no end, and they made the affair of the entire world necessarily as it is by the stars and spheres of conjunction and separation. So we say similarly regarding the stars, and with Allah is success. The Shaykh, may Allah have mercy on him, said: As for the statement about movements with no end, we have already shown its corruption in what preceded. There is no movement that has passed without doubt except that it is an end of the movements that came before, so that nothing of what preceded remains after this one. And if the end of their annihilation and passing is established, it is possible that the effect of what has no beginning comes to an end, so beginning is established for it. Moreover, we see all substances, in the eye's view, having different boundaries. It is not possible that they are so except from a smallest difference that appears in their majority. So it is established that there was for that a smallest gap that becomes greatness and density after it was not, and the fineness of its greatness and density in coming into being after it was not, without anything preceding it; because in preceding there is a requirement of equality, but difference is established. So it is established that what preceded is temporally originated after it was not; since it is in the meaning of what, if the movements were circular, if they were made straight from a direction so that some follow after others, and in the existence of some is the annihilation of others, and if the eternity of movements were necessary to necessitate the eternity of their annihilation, then they would be in pre-eternity non-existent and existent; that is contradictory, for it is not permissible for existence and annihilation to coexist in any state. So likewise in all states, and in that is the necessity of beginning. Moreover, if two things differ in the eye's view in speed of motion, one preceding the other, both moving in a straight line, it is not possible that there is not a beginning for one before the beginning of the other, or that one is faster than the other. And if the end is removed from them, the distinction between them becomes invalid, and in its invalidity is a contradiction of the sensed; so beginning is established for both. And likewise this meaning in circular movements. And with Allah is success. And with all this we refute all those who claim the eternity of entities, which are not beyond accidents. And there is no power except with Allah. And similarly spoke the naturalists.
Source pages p. 742

Commentary
This passage first presents the views of two groups: one that claims the kinds of natures are indefinite and that all things are eternal, and another group of astrologers who claim that stars have always governed the world, with a detailed analogy of a brocade weaver. The astrologers claim bodies are eternal, motions are accidents occurring infinitely, and the world's states are necessitated by stars. Then Maturidi begins his refutation by addressing the claim of infinite motions. He argues: (1) Every motion that has passed has an end, so if motions have an end, they must have a beginning—otherwise, an infinite past could never have reached the present. (2) Substances are observed to have varying boundaries; this implies a smallest part that came into being, proving a beginning. (3) Circular motions, if made straight, would entail that the existence of some motions annihilates others; if motions were eternal, their annihilation would be eternal, leading to the contradiction of being both existent and non-existent in eternity. (4) Two moving objects with different speeds must have beginnings to account for their disparity; otherwise, the sensed distinction would be negated. Thus, all arguments lead to the necessity of a beginning for motions and consequently for the world. This refutes all who claim eternity of entities, including the naturalists.

Key Terms
حركات
نهاية
ابتداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An infinite series of past events can reach the present moment.
Correction: Maturidi argues that if motions had no beginning, they could never end to reach the present, as an infinite series cannot be traversed. Thus, a beginning is necessary.

Checkpoint
What is the core premise of Maturidi's first argument against infinite motions?
A) Motions are caused by stars.
B) Every ended motion implies a starting point.
C) Accidents are eternal.
D) The world is eternal.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's first argument establishes that every motion that ends must have a beginning, refuting the possibility of an infinite past.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that an infinite past is impossible. If your own existence and every moment of your life have a definite beginning, what does that imply about your ultimate purpose and accountability to the One who initiated it?
?
The astrologers attributed the governance of the world to the stars. Are there any influences in your life—people, habits, or circumstances—that you treat as if they have ultimate control over your destiny, instead of recognizing Allah's sovereignty? What would it take for you to realign that perspective today?
?
Maturidi argues that every motion ends, so there must be a beginning. Think of a recurring sin or pattern you have assumed will never end. How does the certainty that all things have a beginning and an end change the urgency with which you should seek to change that pattern?

Proofs from Substances and Circular Motions
Maturidi uses observable properties of substances and logical analysis of circular motion to prove a beginning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's arguments from the varying boundaries of substances and the contradictions in eternal circular motions to prove a beginning.

Core Idea
Observed differences in substances and the logic of circular motion force the conclusion that creation had a beginning.

Maturidi presents two further arguments. First, we see that substances have different boundaries, which implies a smallest part that came into being after not existing. Second, if circular motions were eternal, they would entail the coexistence of existence and annihilation, an absurdity. Both arguments reinforce the necessity of a beginning.

Guided Path
1
Read the substance argument
Read the passage where Maturidi discusses substances (jawahir) having different boundaries. Note how he derives a smallest part from observation.
2
Understand the implication
The varying boundaries require a smallest part that came into being, proving a temporal origin.
3
Read the circular motion argument
Read Maturidi's argument about circular motions. He imagines them made straight to show that if eternal, existence and annihilation would coexist.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the contradiction
Realize that eternal circular motions would require each motion's annihilation to be eternal, leading to the impossible state of being both existent and non-existent in pre-eternity.

وقوم قالوا بمثل ذلك إلا أنهم زعموا أن ليس لأجناس [الطبائع] عدد يعرفونه ، وكلهم قالوا بقدم الأشياء فى جميع جملتها من مهب الشمال والجنوب والدبور والصبا ومن أعلاها وأسفلها متصلة به وزعم قوم من المنجمة أن النجوم لم تزل تدبر أمر العالم ، وهى ومنها سعد ، فاختلافه باختلاف ما اتصل به منها كأداة صاحب الديباج بالخيوط الموصولة من الإبر بسم بأعلى أداتها بما يظهر فيه من الظهور وغيره برفع الخشب وحفظها ، فمثله أمر النجوم بالعالم تختلف صورته باختلاف تحرك النجوم ، وفى اختلافها وائتلافها السعادة والنحس . وهي لم تزل تتحرك فيحدث من كل حركة غير الذي يحدث من غيرها ويتولد ذلك ، ويمثل ذلك يقولون في البيضة والدجاجة أنه يكون ذلك بضرب من حركات النجوم كالديباج الذي ذكرت . وزعموا أن الأجسام قديمة وهى غير الأعراض ، والحركات أعراض ، تحدث إلى ما لا نهاية لها ، وصيروا أمر جميع العالم اضطرارا بما كان كذلك بالنجوم والأفلاك من اجتماع وتفرق ، فمثله في النجوم نقول ، وبالله التوفيق . قال الشيخ رحمه الله : / أما القول بحركات لا نهاية لها فقد بينا فيما تقدم فسادها ، ما لا يشك في حركة انقضت إلا أنها نهاية ما تقدم من الحركات حتى لا يكون شيء مما تقدم بعد هذه ، وإذا ثبت نهاية الفناء لها والانقضاء هو كذلك، يجز أن يتناهى الاقتضاء لما لا يتناهى له الابتداء ، ثبت لذلك الابتداء . وبعد ، فإنا رأينا الجواهر كلها فى رأى العين متفاوتة الحدود ، لا يحتمل أن تكون هي كذلك، على غير أن تكون كذلك إلا عن أقل متفاوت يظهر في أكثره ذلك : فثبت أن كان لذلك عن أصغر خال يكون عظمة وكثافته بعد أن لم يكن ، ولطف عظمه وكثافته في الكون بعد أن لم يكن لا بشيء تقدمه ؛ لأن في التقديم ايجاب الاستواء ، وقد ثبت التفاوت ، فثبت أن الذي تقدم هو حدث بعد أن لم يكن ؛ إذ هو في معنى ما مع ما لو كانت الحركات إذ هي مستديرة لو جعلت مستقيمة من جهة ليكون بعضها على أثر بعض ، وفى وجود بعضها فناء البعض ، ولو وجب قديم الحركات ليجب قدم فنائها ، فتكون في الأزل معدومة موجودة ؛ وذلك متناقض ؛ إذ لا يجوز اجتماع الوجود والفناء في حال ، فكذا فى كل الأحوال ، وفى ذلك لزوم الابتداء . مع ما لو تفاوت - And a group said similarly, except that they claimed that the kinds of [natures] do not have a known number, and all of them said that things are eternal in their entirety, from the direction of the north, south, west, and east winds, and from their highest and lowest parts connected to it. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just seen that the very substances you interact with daily demand a beginning. If everything you own, every atom of your body, was brought into existence from nothing, what claim does your Creator have on your time and attention today? Will you live today as if He created you, or as if you created yourself?
?
The argument about circular motion shows that an eternal cycle of causes without a first cause leads to a logical absurdity. Where in your life are you caught in a cycle of repetition—sin, regret, sin again—that you treat as if it were eternal and unbreakable? What would it mean to acknowledge that a beginning is possible with the first cause who created you?
?
Maturidi forces us to see that without a beginning, existence itself would be contradictory. Your own existence, your deeds, your goals—if they have no beginning in Allah's will, they are meaningless. Have you let your life drift as if it were an eternal mechanical motion without origin or purpose? What specific step will you take today to consciously root your actions in the beginning that Allah granted you?

Proof from Relative Motion and Refutation of Eternity
Maturidi uses relative motion speeds to prove a beginning and then generalizes the refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument from differential speeds in straight line motion to prove a beginning, and how this refutes all who claim eternity of entities.

Core Idea
If two moving objects have different speeds, they must have beginnings to account for their disparity, otherwise the observed difference would be impossible.

Maturidi presents a final argument based on observable motion: if two things move in a straight line with different speeds, one must have started before the other. Removing a beginning would eliminate the distinction, contradicting what we see. This solidifies the case against eternal motions and extends to refute all who claim eternity of entities, including the naturalists.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument on speed difference
Read the passage where Maturidi describes two moving objects with different speeds in a straight line.
2
Understand the implication
The difference in speed implies a beginning for at least one; otherwise, they would be indistinguishable.
3
Read the conclusion
Read how Maturidi concludes that this applies to circular motions as well, and then uses these arguments to refute all who say entities are eternal.
He specifically mentions naturalists.
4
Reflect on the overall refutation
Appreciate how the arguments build a cumulative case for the temporal origin of the world.

Correction: Maturidi argues that without a beginning, the difference in speed and position cannot be accounted for, contradicting observation.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi conclude from the difference in speed between two moving objects?
A) Both are eternal.
B) They must have begun at different times.
C) Speed is an illusion.
D) The naturalists are correct.

Key Takeaway
The observable difference in motion speeds provides a clear proof that motions had a beginning, refuting all claims of eternal entities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You see speed differences every day—cars, runners, the sunrise. Have you ever paused to realize that each such difference silently screams that the universe had a beginning? How does that recognition change your attitude toward the Creator?
?
The proof demolishes the idea that anything could be eternal without a beginning. What in your life have you been treating as if it will last forever—your youth, health, or wealth? When will you begin to live as if only Allah is eternal?
?
Maturidi calls the invalidity of no-beginning a 'contradiction of the sensed.' You trust your senses every moment. Will you trust them today to accept that your own existence has a beginning and an end? What will you do differently once you fully accept that?

Substances Have Varying Limits Proving Creation
Maturidi presents the initial observation and logical deduction about substances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the observed variation in substance sizes implies a smallest created part.

Core Idea
Different limits in substances point to a created smallest unit.

Maturidi begins by making a simple observation: substances (jawahir) are seen to have different sizes and boundaries. He argues that such variation cannot be inherent but must result from a smallest component that came into being. This leads him to conclude that substances are created.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to grasp the initial observation and logical flow.
Note the key terms: جواهر, حدود, تفاوت.
2
Identify the observation and reasoning
Maturidi first states that substances differ in limits. Then he argues that this difference must come from a smallest unit that was not previously there.
3
Connect to the conclusion
Understand that the smallest unit's coming into being from non-existence implies creation. This is the core of the proof.
The smallest unit 'becomes magnitude and density after it was not.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد، فإنا رأينا الجواهر كلها فى رأى العين متفاوتة الحدود، لا يحتمل أن تكون هي كذلك، على غير أن تكون كذلك إلا عن أقل متفاوت يظهر في أكثره ذلك : فثبت أن كان لذلك عن أصغر خال يكون عظمة وكثافته بعد أن لم يكن، ولطف عظمه وكثافته في الكون بعد أن لم يكن لا بشيء تقدمه؛ لأن في التقديم ايجاب الاستواء، وقد ثبت التفاوت، فثبت أن الذي تقدم هو حدث بعد أن لم يكن؛ إذ هو في معنى ما مع ما لو كانت الحركات إذ هي مستديرة لو جعلت مستقيمة من جهة ليكون بعضها على أثر بعض، وفى وجود بعضها فناء البعض، ولو وجب قديم الحركات ليجب قدم فنائها، فتكون في الأزل معدومة موجودة؛ وذلك متناقض؛ إذ لا يجوز اجتماع الوجود والفناء في حال، فكذا فى كل الأحوال، وفى ذلك لزوم الابتداء.
And further, we see that all substances (jawahir) in the eye's view differ in their limits. It is not possible that they are thus except from a smallest difference that appears in their greater part. So it is established that that is due to a smallest [thing] that becomes magnitude and density after it was not, and the subtlety of its magnitude and density in coming into being after not being is not preceded by anything, because precedence necessitates equality, but difference has been established. So it is established that what preceded is an event after it was not, because it is in the sense of what [follows] with the fact that if motions are circular, if they were made straight in some direction so that some follow others, and in the existence of some is the annihilation of others, and if motions were eternal, then their annihilation would be eternal, so they would be in pre-eternity existent and nonexistent; that is contradictory, because existence and annihilation cannot coexist in a state, and likewise in all states, and in that is the necessity of a beginning.
Source pages p. 743

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the creation of substances. The author observes that substances (jawahir) are observed to have varying sizes and limits. This variation cannot be without a smallest unit of difference. The existence of such a smallest unit implies that it came into being from nothing, because its magnitude and density were not before. The argument then extends to motions: if motions were circular and made straight, some would annihilate others. If motions were eternal, their annihilation would also be eternal, leading to the contradiction of simultaneous existence and non-existence. Therefore, a beginning is necessary.

Key Terms
جواهر
حدود
تفاوت
أصغر
عظمة
كثافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Substances could be eternal with varying sizes inherently.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the very fact of variation implies a prior state of non-variation, requiring creation.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the variation in limits of substances imply?
A) Substances are eternal
B) The smallest part must have been created
C) Substances have no smallest part
D) Limits are illusions

Key Takeaway
The observable diversity in substance sizes points to a created smallest unit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the smallest particle in your own body was brought from non-existence, how does that change the way you view your own life? Are you living as if your existence is accidental or as a deliberate creation?
?
The variation in the world around you points to a Creator who designed every detail. Pick one unique trait in yourself—your height, your voice, your mind—and ask yourself: Do I thank the One who gave it to me, or do I take it for granted?
?
The smallest unit had a beginning. That means you, made of such units, are not self-sufficient. Will you live today acknowledging your dependence on your Creator, or will you act as if you are self-made?

Motion Contradiction Proves a Beginning
Maturidi uses a thought experiment on motions to derive a necessary beginning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses a contradiction from eternal motions to prove that the world had a beginning.

Core Idea
Eternal motions lead to contradictory existence and annihilation.

Maturidi extends his argument to motions. He imagines circular motions made straight, where some motions annihilate others. If motions were eternal, both motion and annihilation would coexist, leading to a logical contradiction. Therefore, motions must have a beginning.

Guided Path
1
Read the conditional argument
Read the passage that begins with 'if motions are circular...' and trace the conditional reasoning.
Notice the structure: if A (circular), then B (straight), then C (annihilation).
2
Understand the contradiction
If motions are eternal, annihilation is also eternal, leading to a thing being both existent and nonexistent in pre-eternity.
This contradiction forces the conclusion that motions have a beginning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And further, we see that all substances (jawahir) in the eye's view differ in their limits. It is not possible that they are thus except from a smallest difference that appears in their greater part. So it is established that that is due to a smallest [thing] that becomes magnitude and density after it was not, and the subtlety of its magnitude and density in coming into being after not being is not preceded by anything, because precedence necessitates equality, but difference has been established. So it is established that what preceded is an event after it was not, because it is in the sense of what [follows] with the fact that if motions are circular, if they were made straight in some direction so that some follow others, and in the existence of some is the annihilation of others, and if motions were eternal, then their annihilation would be eternal, so they would be in pre-eternity existent and nonexistent; that is contradictory, because existence and annihilation cannot coexist in a state, and likewise in all states, and in that is the necessity of a beginning.

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the creation of substances. The author observes that substances (jawahir) are observed to have varying sizes and limits. This variation cannot be without a smallest unit of difference. The existence of such a smallest unit implies that it came into being from nothing, because its magnitude and density were not before. The argument then extends to motions: if motions were circular and made straight, some would annihilate others. If motions were eternal, their annihilation would also be eternal, leading to the contradiction of simultaneous existence and non-existence. Therefore, a beginning is necessary.

A) Motions would have no direction

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The argument shows that eternal existence leads to impossibility. What is one such habit, and what step will you take this week to realign it with the reality that you are created and accountable?
?
Maturidi's proof forces you to confront that without a beginning, reason itself collapses. When you avoid thinking about your own beginning (your birth, your creaturely dependence), what contradiction do you introduce into your soul? Write down a prayer of acknowledgment to the Creator that you will recite daily for the next week.

The Brocade Analogy and the Attributes of the Creator
Maturidi uses a parable to introduce attributes of the ultimate planner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses a story about brocade to illustrate the attributes of the ultimate planner and why He must be self-sufficient.

Core Idea
The Creator's self-sufficiency and wisdom are evident from His effortless planning.

Maturidi begins with a parable about a weaver who delegates his work to avoid fatigue. This parable lays the groundwork for the infinite regress argument. In this lesson, we explore the parable and the attributes it reveals about the true Director.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the translation. Let the story and its implication sink in.
2
Understand the story of the brocade
The parable refers to a weaver who could have produced the brocade without fatigue if he had the power. Recognize the implied delegation chain.
This sets up the regress argument.
3
Identify the attributes of the planner
The passage describes the ultimate planner as wise, knowing, and self-sufficient (حكيم, عليم, غني). Note how these attributes are derived from the story.
These attributes are key to the argument.
4
Reflect on the phrase 'لا قوة إلا بالله'
This phrase emphasizes that all power belongs to God alone, reinforcing the self-sufficiency of the ultimate Director.
This phrase is a reminder of tawheed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيكون بتدبير غيرها كان الذي كان، على ما ذكر من قصة الديباج. على يعلم أنه لو قدر على ذلك بلا اتعاب نفسه لاختاره عليه ليعلم أن كل ذلك الأشياء بتدبير حكيم عليم غني استعمل جميع ما ذكر فيما ذكر، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وبعد، فإنه لو جاز القول في عالمنا إنه بتدبير من ذكر لجاز مثله فيمن ذكر أنه كان بتدبير من يعلوه، كذلك إلى ما لا نهاية له، وفي ذلك بطلان قولهم في تدبير النجوم، أو يرجع إلى نهاية وفي ذلك فساد قولهم في رفع النهاية عن وإيجاب القول بواحد إليه يرجع تدبير جميع ما ذكر، وهو العالم بعواقب الأمور المقدر في كل ما إليه ينتهي.
So it would be by the planning of another that what happened happened, as mentioned in the story of the brocade. For he knows that if he were able to do that without fatiguing himself, he would have chosen it over it, so that he knows that all those things are by the planning of a wise, knowing, self-sufficient one who employed all that was mentioned in that which was mentioned. And there is no power except with God. And after that, if it were permissible to say concerning our world that it is by the planning of one mentioned, then the like would be permissible concerning him who was mentioned that he was by the planning of one above him, and so on ad infinitum. In that is the invalidation of their statement concerning the governance of the stars, or it ends at an end, and in that is the corruption of their statement in negating the end and necessitating the statement of one to whom the planning of all that was mentioned returns—and He is the knower of the consequences of affairs, the determiner in everything to which it ends.
Source pages p. 744

Commentary
This passage contains a classic infinite regress argument (tasalsul). Maturidi first makes a point about a hypothetical scenario (story of brocade) to show that if the agent could achieve the result without self-fatigue, He would. Then he applies the regress: if we say that our world is governed by a certain director (e.g., the stars), then that director itself would require a higher director, and so on. This leads to two possibilities: either an infinite chain (la nihaya) or a final end (nihaya). An infinite regress is absurd (bāṭil) and invalidates their claim. If it ends, then that final director must be one (wāḥid) to whom all planning returns. That director is the All-Knowing of consequences, the Determiner (muqaddir) of everything. Thus Maturidi establishes the necessity of a single ultimate Governor, refuting both the astrology of the stars and the naturalism of independent natures.

Key Terms
حكيم
عليم
غني
قصة الديباج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the story is about laziness or delegation being inherently bad.
Correction: The story is used to argue that a truly powerful being would not need subordinates; delegation implies limitation, so the ultimate planner must be self-sufficient.

Checkpoint
What does the parable of the brocade demonstrate about the ultimate planner?
A) He delegates to avoid work
B) He is self-sufficient and able without fatigue
C) He is merely a first mover
D) The planner is unknown

Key Takeaway
The infinite regress argument begins with the intuition that a truly powerful creator would not need subordinates unless He is limited.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel overwhelmed by responsibilities, do you truly believe that all power comes from the Self-Sufficient (الغني)? How would your day change if you repeated 'لا قوة إلا بالله' with full conviction?
?
The passage suggests that the ultimate planner employs means without need. In what area of your life do you rely on your own efforts while forgetting that the true source is God? What is one practical step you can take to shift that reliance today?
?
Do you ever delegate tasks out of a sense of limitation, fearing you cannot do it all? How does knowing that God delegates out of wisdom, not weakness, challenge your own view of delegation? Write one concrete way you can imitate this attribute in a leadership role this week.

Infinite Regress Necessitates a Single Ultimate Director
Maturidi presents the infinite regress argument and its conclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the infinite regress argument and how it leads to the conclusion of a single ultimate director.

Core Idea
An infinite chain of directors is absurd; only one ultimate director can end the regress.

After the parable, Maturidi presents the core infinite regress argument. He shows that positing a chain of directors leads to an absurd infinity or forces an end. This end must be one, eternal, and all-knowing.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the conditional 'if it were permissible' and the two possibilities.
2
Identify the regress structure
Maturidi argues that if the world is directed by X, then X is directed by Y, and so on. Recognize the chain.
3
Analyze the first possibility: infinite regress
An infinite chain is invalid because it leads to no beginning, invalidating the claim that stars govern.
4
Analyze the second possibility: an end
If the chain ends, the claim of no end is corrupted, and we must affirm one ultimate director.
5
Describe the attributes of the ultimate director
The passage describes Him as the knower of consequences and the determiner of everything.
This aligns with the attributes from lesson 1.

?

?
This lesson argues that an infinite chain of directors is absurd. How can you shift your trust from the chain to its single end?
?

The Necessity of a Single Wise Director
Maturidi argues for a single ultimate director and refutes infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the universe must have a single, wise ultimate director, and how he refutes the possibility of an infinite chain of managers.

Core Idea
The universe's wise order demands a single ultimate director, not an infinite regress.

Maturidi begins by establishing that the wise Creator employed means (like the brocade story) to demonstrate His wisdom, even though He could have done without them. He then presents a powerful dilemma against those who attribute the world's management to multiple causes: either the chain of directors goes on forever (absurd), or it terminates in a single wise director. This passage thus affirms monotheism and refutes polytheistic or astrological causation. Let's examine his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic text and its literal English translation. Note the key terms like تدبير (management) and نهاية (end).
The passage is concise; read it twice to grasp the flow.
2
Identify the two main parts
The passage has two clear sections: first, the wise director's use of means to show wisdom; second, the dilemma against multiple directors leading to infinite regress or a single end.
3
Understand the dilemma
Maturidi argues that if you claim the world is managed by some being, then that being itself must be managed by another, leading to an infinite chain. This chain is impossible because it would imply no real director.
Infinite regress is a classic philosophical problem.
4
Conclude with the single director
The only valid alternative is that the chain terminates in a single, wise director who knows all outcomes and decrees all things.
This director is Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على يعلم أنه لو قدر على ذلك بلا اتعاب نفسه لاختاره عليه ليعلم أن كل ذلك أنه الأشياء بتدبير حكيم عليم غنى استعمل جميع ما ذكر فيما ذكر، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وبعد، فإنه لو جاز القول في عالمنا إنه بتدبير من ذكر لجاز مثله فيمن ذكر أنه كان بتدبير من يعلوه، كذلك إلى ما لا نهاية له، وفي ذلك بطلان قولهم في تدبير النجوم، أو يرجع إلى نهاية وفي ذلك فساد قولهم في رفع النهاية وإيجاب القول بواحد إليه يرجع تدبير جميع ما ذكر، وهو العالم بعواقب الأمور المقدر في كل ما إليه ينتهي.
He knows that if He were able to do that without tiring Himself, He would have chosen it over it, so that he knows that all that is that things are by the management of a Wise, Knowing, Self-sufficient One who employed all that was mentioned in what was mentioned, and there is no power except by God. And then, if it were permissible to say in our world that it is by the management of someone mentioned, then the same would be permissible regarding that mentioned one, that he was under the management of one above him, likewise to infinity, and in that is the invalidity of their statement regarding the management of the stars, or it leads to an end, and in that is the corruption of their statement in removing the end and affirming the statement of a single One to whom the management of all that has been mentioned returns, and He is the Knower of the consequences of affairs, the Determiner of everything that ends in Him.
Source pages p. 745

Commentary
This passage is a combined proof and refutation. It first establishes that the wise creator used means (like the story of the brocade) to show His wisdom, since He could have done without them. Then it presents a dilemma against those who attribute the world's management to multiple causes (like stars or subordinate directors): either the chain of directors goes on infinitely (which is absurd and invalidates their claim about the stars), or it terminates in a single ultimate director. The latter is required, and that director is omniscient and decrees all things. The passage thus affirms tawhid and refutes polytheistic or astrological causation.

Key Terms
تدبير
حكيم عليم غني
نهاية
نجوم
واحد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Maturidi's argument only applies to celestial beings like stars, but it is a general refutation of any intermediary causation that implies infinite regress.
Correction: The argument refutes any claim that the universe is managed by a chain of directors, whether they are angels, stars, or any other beings. It affirms that only Allah is the ultimate manager of all affairs.

Checkpoint
What does the passage conclude about the management of the universe?
A) It is the result of random chance.
B) It must have a single ultimate director.
C) It is managed by the stars.
D) It is an infinite chain of managers.

Key Takeaway
The universe must have a single, wise ultimate director; otherwise, infinite regress would render all management meaningless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own life, do you act as if there is a single ultimate Director who knows the consequences of all your affairs? How does that affect your daily decisions? Will you commit to acknowledging that Director before making a major choice this week?
?
The passage argues that infinite regress is invalid. In what areas of your life do you rely on endless secondary causes without turning to the ultimate Cause? What specific step can you take to cut that regress and direct your trust to the One?
?
The text says that if multiple directors were possible, then each would need a director above it. Have you ever tried to serve multiple 'directors' in your life—like wealth, status, or desires—thinking they are independent? How does this argument challenge that? What will you do to align yourself under the single Wise Director?

Diverse Actions Require a Wise Creator
Maturidi proves actions cannot stem from blind nature but from a wise creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the diversity of actions in the world cannot be attributed to blind nature but necessitates a knowing and wise creator.

Core Idea
Opposite effects cannot come from a single blind nature; they demand a wise creator.

This passage from Imam Maturidi presents a concise but powerful argument from the diversity of observed actions. He points out that if the world's processes were driven by blind natures, we would see uniform effects, but we see opposites like heating and cooling, good and evil. This contradiction leads to the conclusion that the ultimate source is a knowing, wise Creator who intentionally creates each thing.

Guided Path
1
Read the original passage
Start by reading the Arabic sentence and its literal translation. Notice the key terms: 'tab‘' (nature), 'af‘āl' (actions), 'tabdīd wa taskhīn' (cooling and heating), 'sharr wa khayr' (evil and good).
The passage is a single, tightly reasoned argument.
2
Understand the logical structure
Identify the premise: actions are diverse. Then the impossibility: such diversity cannot come from a blind nature. Then the conclusion: the source must be a knowing, wise creator.
This is a simple but rigorous proof by contradiction.
3
Reflect on the examples
Consider why Maturidi chose 'cooling and heating' and 'evil and good'. They represent physical and moral opposites. Ask yourself: could a single blind nature produce both heat and cold? Why not?
If nature were the ultimate cause, it would produce only one effect consistently.
4
Connect to the learning objective
Now combine your understanding: the diversity of actions proves that the world is not self-caused by blind natures but is the work of a wise creator who intentionally assigns properties to each thing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد، فإن خروج الأفعال المختلفة وأحوالها محال وجودها من ذي طبع كالتبريد والتسخين والشر والخير، فثبت أن ليس أصل شيء منه بذي طبع ولكن بعليم حكيم جعل كل شيء على ذلك بالخلقة والوجود.
And then, the emergence of different actions and their states is impossible to exist from a thing having a nature (tab‘), like cooling and heating, evil and good. So it is established that the origin of none of that is from a thing having a nature, but from a Knowing, Wise One who made everything upon that by creation and existence.
Source pages p. 745

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the diversity of actions and states in the world. The author argues that if actions originated from a blind nature (like fire naturally heating), they would be uniform. But we observe opposite actions (cooling vs. heating, good vs. evil) coming from the same or similar sources. This impossibility shows that the source is not a blind nature but a knowing, wise agent who intentionally creates each thing with its specific properties.

Key Terms
طبَع
أفعال
تبريد
تسخين
شر
خير
خلقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think 'nature' (tab‘) refers to the essence of a thing, so that if actions come from the nature of a thing, then nature itself is the ultimate cause.
Correction: Maturidi is not denying that things have natures; he is denying that blind natures are the ultimate source of actions. The diversity of actions shows that no single blind nature can be the cause; rather, a wise creator assigns these natures.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that actions cannot come from a blind nature (tab‘)?
A) Because nature is not eternal.
B) Because opposite actions like heating and cooling cannot originate from the same nature.
C) Because nature is created by God.
D) Because actions are only from human will.

Key Takeaway
The diversity of actions in the world, including opposites like heating and cooling, good and evil, cannot originate from a blind nature but must come from a knowing, wise Creator who intentionally gives each thing its properties.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a day filled with both blessings and hardships, do you truly believe that both come from the same wise Creator? Or do you attribute the good to your own efforts and the bad to blind circumstance?
?
If you truly internalized that even evil and good are intentionally created by a Knowing, Wise One, how would your response to suffering change? Would you still despair, or would you seek wisdom behind opposites?
?
Are you living as if the diversity in your life—your joys and trials—comes from a blind, meaningless process, or from a Creator who made everything by creation and existence? What would change if you fully owned the latter?

The Philosophers' Self-Contradiction and Annihilation
Maturidi shows the transformation from eternal essence to multiple atoms leading to annihilation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi exposes the philosophers' self-contradiction: their eternal first principle, which cannot receive accidents, is turned into atoms, leading to its own annihilation.

Core Idea
The philosophers' eternal substance cannot survive their own logic.

Maturidi continues his refutation by showing that the philosophers' starting point—an eternal essence beyond accidents—inevitably leads to its own destruction when they turn it into jawāhir. This exposes a fundamental flaw in their system.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Pay attention to the sequence of transformations Maturidi describes.
Notice the repeated 'ثم' indicating a step-by-step reduction.
2
Identify the transformation
Maturidi says the philosophers made the eternal entity incapable of receiving accidents, then made it a jawhar, then jawāhir. Mark these three stages.
3
Understand the consequence
The original entity vanishes, leaving only jawāhir and accidents. This implies the annihilation of the world by itself, contradicting their intent.
This consequence is the key refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذ صيروا الذي لذاته خارج عن احتمال الأعراض ممتنع عن معنى الجواهر ثم جوهرا ثم جواهر، ثم صار بحيث لم يبق من أوليته أثر، وما بقى مما انتهى أمر العالم من القديم والحديث إلا الجواهر والأعراض، وذهب الذي لم يكن بهذا الوصف، فيكون في ذلك فناء العالم بنفسه، واستحالة القديم بذاته بأعراض قهرته وأفنته مما لا قيام لها بنفسها. ويكون في ذلك القول بحدث ويكون في ذلك القول بحدث جميع العالم، الذي دفعهم عظم هذا القول إلى ذلك الخيال؛ إذ كل ما هو مأخوذ إنما هو عرض وجوهر، ولم يكن الأول، ثم يبطل قوله إذا سمى نفسه حكيما ألزم غيره الصدود عن رأيه واتباع هواه بعد قوله: إن الأصل الذي منه كان جاهلا سفيها، وأن الأعراض هي أغيار ولدتها القوة السقيمة التي لا حكمة فيها ولا علم لديها أحد أبنائها الذي لم ينل شيئا إلا بها، فمن أين قدم نفسه عليها. وإذا جاز من غير أصل له به، صار كذلك، فليقل في جميع العالم بمثل الذي قال بنفسه.
For they made that which in its essence is beyond the reception of accidents, incapable of the meaning of jawāhir, then a jawhar, then jawāhir. Then it came to such a state that no trace of its primacy remained. Nothing remained of what the affair of the world ended in, of the eternal and the temporal, except jawāhir and accidents. And that which was not with this description [the eternal prime] vanished. Thus there would be in that the annihilation of the world by itself, and the changing of the eternal in its essence by accidents that overpowered it and annihilated it, which have no subsistence by themselves. And in that there would be the affirmation of origination (ḥudūth), and in that there would be the affirmation of the origination of the entire world – which is what the enormity of this statement drove them to that fantasy. For everything that is assumed is only accident and jawhar, and the first does not exist. Then his statement is invalidated when he calls himself wise but compels others to turn away from his opinion and follow their desire, after his statement that the origin from which [he came] was ignorant and foolish, and that the accidents are others (aghyār) born of the sickly power which has no wisdom nor knowledge in it – one of its progeny who attained nothing except through it. So from where did he place himself above them? And if it is possible without an origin to him, then it is so; let him say concerning the entire world the like of what he said about himself.
Source pages p. 747

Commentary
This passage continues the refutation by exposing a fundamental contradiction: the philosophers begin with an eternal, immutable first principle (the hyle) that cannot receive accidents, yet they turn it into a jawhar (atom) and then multiple jawāhir, losing all trace of the original. All that remains are jawāhir and accidents, implying the annihilation of the original eternal entity. This, Maturidi argues, actually demonstrates the origination of the entire world (ḥudūth), which they sought to avoid. He then attacks their inconsistency: they call themselves wise but derive everything from an ignorant, foolish origin. The power they posit is sickly, without wisdom or knowledge. Thus, their claim to wisdom is baseless. If one could assume origination without a cause, then one could just as well say the world is created by itself, which is absurd.

Key Terms
جوهر
عرض
فناء
قدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the philosophers' view preserves an eternal first principle.
Correction: Maturidi shows that by turning it into multiple atoms, the original eternal entity is annihilated.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say happens to the original eternal entity in the philosophers' view?
A) It becomes the soul of the world.
B) It vanishes leaving only jawāhir and accidents.
C) It remains unchanged.
D) It becomes a contingent being.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that the philosophers' own logic forces the annihilation of their primary substance, exposing a contradiction at the heart of their system.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there any belief about Allah that you hold which, if you followed its logical threads, would ultimately dissolve into contradiction? Are you willing to examine it with the same rigor Maturidi applies to the philosophers?
?
Maturidi shows how the philosophers' first principle was gradually emptied of its essence until nothing of its original remained. Have you allowed external influences or careless reasoning to erode core tenets of your faith, step by step, without noticing the loss?
?
The philosophers' system collapsed because it began with a premise incompatible with its later moves. What premise in your own understanding of tawḥīd might be subtly inconsistent with the way you actually live or think about Allah? Will you commit to resolving it today?

The Implication of Origination and the Inconsistency of Wisdom
Maturidi concludes that the philosophers' view implies the world's origination and then attacks their claim to wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi argues that the philosophers' view actually proves the origination (ḥudūth) of the world, and why their claim to wisdom is self-defeating.

Core Idea
Their system proves creation but undermines their own wisdom.

Having exposed the annihilation of the prime substance, Maturidi now draws the conclusion: this entails the origination of the entire world, exactly what the philosophers sought to avoid. He then attacks their inconsistency in claiming wisdom while deriving everything from an ignorant origin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the transition from the previous argument to the conclusion about ḥudūth.
The passage starts with 'ويكون في ذلك' linking to the prior content.
2
Identify the conclusion about origination
Maturidi says their view leads to the affirmation of ḥudūth of the entire world, which they were trying to avoid.
3
Analyze the attack on their claim to wisdom
Maturidi points out the irony: they call themselves wise but their origin is ignorant and foolish. Ask yourself: how can wisdom come from ignorance?
This is a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

For they made that which in its essence is beyond the reception of accidents, incapable of the meaning of jawāhir, then a jawhar, then jawāhir. The Power's Authority and Direct Creation
Maturidi questions the power's autonomy and argues for God's direct creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that if a power can transform the primal matter (hyle), then that power must be attributed to God's direct creation.

Core Idea
If a power can transform matter, God can originate it.

Maturidi presents a concise yet powerful argument against the philosophers' view that the hyle (primal matter) is self-sufficient. He reasons that the power causing its transformation must have authority over it, and thus we should acknowledge that God directly created the hyle. This lesson unpacks this argument and its implications for divine causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the fragment
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the conditional structure: 'then the power... cannot be free from having authority'.
The text is fragmentary, but the logical skeleton is clear.
2
Trace the logical move
Identify the key terms: 'power' (quwwa), 'hyle' (hayūlā), 'authority' (sulṭān), and 'originated' (ansha'a). Follow the reasoning: if a power turns the hyle, it must have authority; therefore, one should say God originated the hyle.
Maturidi is turning the philosophers' own premise against them.
3
Reflect on the argument's strength
Consider why Maturidi insists on direct creation (inshā'). The argument implies that admitting an efficient cause for change in matter already entails a creator of matter itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لا يخلو القوة التي في قلبت الحيولي من أن يكون ذا سلطان عليها بمائها قلبتها، فليقل هو في الله سبحانه أنشأ الهيولى أو ما شاء على وجه، ...
Then the power that turned the hyle cannot be free from having authority over it by its essence, it turned it. So let him say concerning God, exalted, that He originated the hyle or whatever He willed in some manner...
Source pages p. 747

Commentary
This fragment presents a final argument: the power that causes the transformation of the hyle must itself have authority over it. If the philosophers admit that such a power can act on the hyle, then one should simply attribute the origin of the hyle itself to God's direct creation (inshāʾ). The argument is incomplete in the surviving text, but the intent is clear: the philosophers' own logic leads to positing a powerful agent, which is God.

Key Terms

هيولى
سلطان
أنشأ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The hyle is self-sufficient.
B) God originated the hyle.
C) The power is the only creator.
D) The world is eternal.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi uses the philosophers' own assumption about a transforming power to argue that God directly created the primal matter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You witness changes in your body, your circumstances, and the world around you every day. If even a small power that transforms matter points to a Creator with authority, what does every change in your life say about God? Are you responding to these constant signs with submission, or do you take them for granted?
?
The philosophers acknowledged a power that changes the hyle but stopped short of attributing the origin of matter to God. Is there an area in your life where you admit a higher power exists but hesitate to fully surrender that area to God? What is the cost of that hesitation?
?
Maturidi's argument forces you to either attribute the origination of all things to God or to leave a gap in your reasoning. Have you ever honestly confronted the question of why there is something rather than nothing? If not, what are you afraid of finding?

The Incoherence of an Eternal Inherent Power in Matter
Maturidi refutes the materialist claim using the eternity argument and accident dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the materialist claim that an inherent power in matter causes change leads to contradictions about eternity and the origin of accidents.

Core Idea
A natural power cannot remain idle for eternity.

Imam al-Maturidi begins his refutation by focusing on a fatal flaw in the materialist theory: if an inherent power (quwwa) in matter is natural and inseparable, why did it not act before the world existed? This passage exposes the contradiction and also shows that the existence of accidents further undermines the materialist position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic once, then the translation. Notice how Maturidi contrasts the eternity argument with the observed world.
2
Identify the two main arguments
First, the argument from eternity: if the power is natural, it should have acted from eternity. Second, the argument from accidents: either they were eternally in matter or came from nothing.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why Maturidi calls this a refutation. How does it show the need for a Creator?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيقبل التقليب ويقوم به التركيب، ثم ليسم بما شاء هو على فناء ما قلبها فإذا بطل الأصل الذي به العالم وهلك، مع الإحالة أن يهلك القائم بذاته ليكون بهلاكه انقلاب غير وقيامه، مع ما يكون في الهيولى تلفها، فتصير هي بلا قوة التقليب، فيكون في ذلك إبطال العالم وتقلبه من حال إلى حال دائما، فدل وجوده على فساد هذا الأصل. مع ما في الشاهد أن لا يوجد شيء يصير بحيث لم يكن يصلح إلا بحكيم يجعله كذلك، فثبت أن ابتداء العالم إن صلح أن يحتمل كون هذه الجواهر والأعراض كان كذلك، كل على جعله يصلح لشيء كذلك و بعد، فإن القوة إذ هي قلبته بالطبع فهي غير مفارقة عنه، فما بالها خلت عن عملها في القدم، وذو الطبع لا يخلو عن عمله في الشاهد. على أن الأعراض التي أحدثت إما أن كانت في الهيولى فيبطل قوله: كانت خالية عنها حتى حدثت، أو لم يكن فحدثت من غير شيء؛ إذ وصف القوة بما وصف به الهيولى، ولم يكن فيه أعراض، فثبت أيضا كونها لا عن شيء، وهذا المعنى الزمهم بالقول الذي قالوا، فبطل بحمد الله. على أنه أمكن القلب عليهم في كل ما قالوا للقوة أن يجعل ذلك للهيولى في القوة، على أنها لا تخلو من غير أن يكون غير الهيولى، فها اثنان، وزعم الكم من باب العدد، فلم يكن فلم يكن ثمة حدث، وقد أوجب هنالك، أو هي هيولى. فيبطل قوله: هي مع الهيولى، أو هي التي قلبت الهيولى، وكأنها قلبت نفسها لا الهيولى. مع ما زعم أن تلك الأعراض اعترضت في الهيولى فحركته وسكنته ودفعته وخفضته من غير أن كان ثمة غير إليه تتحرك أو فيه يسكن أو إليه يرتفع وينحط، ووجود أمثال فاسد فما عنه تولده، فهي في أصله أشد فسادا. وزعم محمد بن شبيب أنه يسمى القوة حركة، وفي روايته أنها لا توصف بما لا توصف به الهيولى، وقد ذكر عنهم الآراء في الهيولى، فلا أدري أيصح ذا أو لا؟ إلا أن سمى القوة حركة وهي فيه، فيبطل قوله: إن الهيولى لا يوصف بحركة إذ قد وصفه بها. لا يتجلو من أن يكون مماسة له أو مباينة عنه، وأيهما قال، فيه إثبات الجسمية والعرضية؛ إذ البينونة والمماسة غير الذي يماس ويباين. ثم قول هؤلاء أن حدثت الجواهر من حركات الأصل، وكذلك قول المنجمة، ومعلوم وجود جواهر من علو وسفل ومن كل جانب، على إحالة تلك الحركات المختلفة، فثبت أن ذا باطل. وبهذا الفصل ناقضهم النظام: إنه إذا كان بقلب القوة الهيولى سبب حدوث الأعراض، ثم هي تختلف كاللون والطعم والحر واللين ونحو ذلك، فيحدث ذلك كله في وقت واحد وبحركة إنما هي تكون من جهة واحدة. فقيل: تكون من جهات. فزعم أن أكثرها ستة، وقد يحدث الشر من اثنى عشر من تلك الأعراض، فثبت أن ذلك لتقليب القوة. على أن التقليب يكون من جهة، والأعراض تكثر، ثبت أن ذلك ليس بما ذكر. وعارفهم محمد بن شبيب بما الهيولى قبل حدوث الأعراض ليست بطويلة والأعراض ليست بطويلة فكيف صارت عند الوجود طويلة؟ وكذلك العرض، ولو جاز ذا لجاز أن يجمع بين ما ليس يخلو وما لا يخلو، فيصير خلو، ومثله في جميع الأعراض كلا سواد ولا سواد.
So it accepts turning and composition occurs through it, then let it be named whatever it wishes upon the destruction of what it turned. For if the principle by which the world exists is nullified and perishes, along with the impossibility that the self-subsistent perishes such that its perishing is an inversion of its other and its subsistence, along with what occurs in matter (hayula) of its destruction, so it becomes devoid of the power of turning. Thus in that is the nullification of the world and its perpetual turning from state to state. So its existence indicates the corruption of this principle. Along with what is observed, that nothing exists that becomes such as it was not, except through a wise being who makes it so. Thus it is established that the beginning of the world, if it is possible to contain these substances (jawāhir) and accidents (aʿrāḍ), was such, each according to its maker making it suitable for something. Then moreover, since the power (quwwa) turns it by nature, it is inseparable from it. So why was it devoid of its action in eternity? For that which has a nature is not devoid of its action in the observed world. And also the accidents that were produced either were in matter, then his statement is nullified that it was devoid of them until they occurred, or they were not, then they occurred from nothing, since power is described as matter is described, and there were no accidents in it. So it is also established that they occur from nothing, and this meaning coerces them by the statement they said. So it is nullified, praise be to God. Moreover, it is possible to turn their argument against them in everything they said: that power could be attributed to matter in the power, as it is not devoid of something other than matter, so there are two entities. And they claimed quantity from the category of number, so there was no event, yet he necessitated something there, or it is matter. So his statement is nullified: it is with matter, or it is what turned matter, as if it turned itself, not matter. Along with his claim that those accidents occurred in matter, moving it, making it still, pushing it, lowering it, without there being another to which it moves or in which it rests or to which it rises and descends. And the existence of such things is corrupt, so what is generated from it is even more corrupt in its origin. Muhammad ibn Shabib claimed that he calls the power 'motion', and in his narration it is not described with what matter is not described. And he mentioned from them opinions about matter, so I do not know if this is correct or not. Except that he named the power 'motion' while it is in it, so his statement is nullified that matter is not described with motion, since he has described it with it. It cannot avoid being either contiguous to it or separate from it. Whichever he says, in it is the affirmation of corporeality (jismiyya) and accidentiality (ʿaraḍiyya), since separation and contiguity are other than that which separates and is contiguous. Then the statement of these people that substances occurred from the motions of the origin, and likewise the statement of the astrologers, while it is known that substances exist from above and below and from every side, despite the impossibility of those diverse motions. So it is established that this is false. And by this section al-Nazzām refuted them: if by the turning of power matter is the cause of the occurrence of accidents, then they differ like color, taste, heat, softness and the like, then all that occurs at one time and by a motion that comes only from one direction. So it was said: they come from directions. He claimed that most of them are six, and sometimes evil occurs from twelve of those accidents. So it is established that that is due to the turning of power. Since the turning is from one direction, and the accidents are many, it is established that that is not as he mentioned. And Muhammad ibn Shabib argued against them: if matter before the occurrence of accidents is not long, and accidents are not long, how did it become long upon existence? Likewise the accident. And if this were permissible, it would be permissible to combine that which is not devoid and that which is not devoid, resulting in devoidness. And the like in all accidents: neither blackness nor non-blackness.
Source pages p. 748

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the materialist theory that an inherent power (quwwa) in primordial matter (hayula) causes change and the generation of the world. Imam al-Maturidi systematically dismantles this claim by showing its internal contradictions. First, he argues that if the world is composed of a power that turns matter, then the world would be subject to perpetual destruction and change, but its actual existence indicates a wise maker, not a blind power. Second, he questions why the power, if it is inseparable from matter by nature, did not act from eternity—since in the observed world, a natural power never remains idle. Third, he examines the production of accidents: either they existed in matter from eternity (contradicting the claim that matter was originally devoid of them) or they occurred from nothing (which implies creation ex nihilo, something the materialists deny). He then turns the argument against them: if power is described as matter is, it becomes a second entity, leading to an infinite regress or to the absurdity that power turns itself. Next, he addresses Muhammad ibn Shabib's identification of power with motion, showing that if motion is in matter, then matter becomes subject to motion, contradicting the claim that matter is not described by motion. He concludes that matter either is contiguous to motion or separate, both of which imply corporeality and accidentality. Finally, he cites al-Nazzām's objection: if turning power causes diverse accidents like color, taste, etc., they would all occur at once from a single motion, but observation shows they differ and come from multiple directions. Muhammad ibn Shabib also argues that matter and accidents are not long individually, yet combined they become long—this absurdity shows the theory fails. The overall point is that the materialist explanation is incoherent, and the existence of the world points to a wise Creator.

Key Terms
قوة (quwwa)
هيولى (hayula)
أعراض (aʿrāḍ)
قدم (qidam)
شاهد (shāhid)
طبع (ṭabʿ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidi denies all natural causation.
Correction: Maturidi is not denying secondary causality per se; he is refuting a specific atheistic model where matter has an inherent self-sufficient power. He does accept that Allah creates through means.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why does the materialist claim that quwwa is natural and inseparable from matter lead to a contradiction?
A) Because the power is not observable.
B) Because the power should have acted from eternity but the world is created in time.
C) Because matter cannot have accidents.
D) Because the power is separate from matter.

Key Takeaway
The materialist claim that an inherent power in matter causes change fails because it cannot explain why the power was inactive before the world began.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The materialist believes matter can move itself. But what do your own habits reveal? Are you moving toward Allah by your own nature, or do you need constant divine turning? What is that one habit you have left idle for far too long, and why haven't you changed it yet?
?
Maturidi says a natural power cannot be idle. Think about the power Allah has placed within you—your intellect, your desire for truth, your ability to act. Have you left that power unused in your spiritual life? What would it mean to finally let it move you toward sincere worship today?
?
If the world's existence proves materialism false, then your existence also screams 'Creator.' Are you listening? Right now, what is the one belief or action in your life that still pretends the universe runs on its own, ignoring the One who holds you in existence every moment? What will you do about it before you sleep tonight?

Turning the Tables: Refuting Materialist Positions on Power and Motion
Maturidi refutes materialist positions on power and motion, including those of Muhammad ibn Shabib and al-Nazzām.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi turns the materialist arguments against themselves and refutes specific claims by Muhammad ibn Shabib and al-Nazzām.

Core Idea
If power is described as matter, it becomes a second entity — an infinite regress arises.

Having shown the incoherence of the inherent power theory, Maturidi now attacks the materialist claims from another angle. He demonstrates that if power is understood as a quality of matter, it becomes a separate entity, leading to absurdities. He then refutes specific attempts by Muhammad ibn Shabib to identify power with motion and al-Nazzām's objection about diverse accidents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, paying attention to the logical turns Maturidi makes.
2
Follow the refutation of Muhammad ibn Shabib
Notice how Maturidi shows that if power is motion, then matter would be described by motion, contradicting the claim that matter lacks motion.
3
Examine al-Nazzām's objection and the final argument
See how Maturidi uses the diversity of accidents from a single motion to refute the materialist model.
